## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Cross-Org gRPC Service Definition Discovery

## Your Task

Find the gRPC service definitions that are shared between `envoyproxy/envoy` and `grpc/grpc`. Specifically: 1. In `envoyproxy/data-plane-api`, find all `.proto` files that define `service` declarations using `rpc` methods (the xDS service definitions). 2. In `grpc/grpc`, find the source files that implement the `grpc_health_v1.Health` service (the standard gRPC health checking protocol). Report the repo, file path, and service name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

It compliments Envoy\u2019s health checking\\n27: // service by designating this Envoy to be a healthchecker for a subset of hosts\\n28: // in the cluster. The status of these health checks will be reported to the\\n29: // management server, where it can be aggregated etc and redistributed back to\\n30: // Envoy through EDS.\\n31: service HealthDiscoveryService {\\n32:   // 1. Envoy starts up and if its can_healthcheck option in the static\\n33:   //    bootstrap config is enabled, sends HealthCheckRequest to the management\\n34:   //    server. It streams\\n39:   //    HealthCheckSpecifier messages with cluster related configuration for all\\n40:   //    clusters this Envoy is designated to health check. Subsequent\\n41:   //    HealthCheckSpecifier message will be sent on changes to:\\n42:   //    a. Endpoints to health checks\\n43:   //    b. Per cluster configuration change\\n44:   // 3. Based on the HealthCheck\\n46:   //    configuration Envoy waits upon the arrival of the probe response and\\n47:   //    looks at the content of the response to decide whether the endpoint is\\n48:   //    healthy or not. If a response hasn't been received within the timeout\\n49:   //    interval, the endpoint health status is considered TIMEOUT.\\n50:   // 4. Envoy reports results back in an EndpointHealthResponse message.\\n51:   //    Envoy streams responses as often as the interval configured by the\\n52:   //    management server in HealthCheckSpecifier.\\n53:   // 5. The management Server collects health statuses for all endpoints in the\\n54:   //    cluster (for all clusters) and uses this information to construct\\n55:   //    EndpointDiscoveryResponse messages.\\n56:   // 6. Once Envoy has a list of upstream endpoints to send traffic to, it load\\n57:   //    balances traffic to them without additional health checking. It may\\n58:   //    use inline healthcheck (i.e. consider endpoint UNHEALTHY if connection\\n59:   //    failed to a particular endpoint to account for health status propagation\\n60:   //    delay between HDS and EDS).\\n61:   // By default, can_healthcheck is true. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\\n36: // 4. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n30: // 2. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\n44: //\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\n50:   // protocol is described by the ``ProcessingRequest`` and ``ProcessingResponse``\n51: ",
    "url": "https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367@d9596a37e1620efc399ac5ce4821e268985e7dcc/-/blob/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto%3FL1-50"
  }
